<p><b>Fußball-Club Bayern München e.V.</b>, commonly known as <b>FC Bayern München</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[ʔɛf tseː ˈbaɪɐn ˈmʏnçn̩]</a></span>), <b>FCB</b>, <b>Bayern Munich</b>, or <b>FC Bayern</b>, is a German <a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">sports club</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, Germany. It is best known for its professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team, which plays in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>, the top tier of the <a href="/wiki/German_football_league_system" title="German football league system">German football league system</a>, and is the most successful club in German football history, having won a record 26 <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">national titles</a> and 18 <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">national cups</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>FC Bayern was founded in 1900 by 11 football players, led by <a href="/wiki/Franz_John" title="Franz John">Franz John</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcbbook1stch_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-fcbbook1stch-4">[4]</a></sup> Although Bayern won its first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_football_champions" title="German football champions">national championship</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_football_championship_1932" title="German football championship 1932">1932</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory0045_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory0045-5">[5]</a></sup> the club was not selected for the Bundesliga at <a href="/wiki/Introduction_of_the_Bundesliga" title="Introduction of the Bundesliga">its inception in 1963</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nobl_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-nobl-6">[6]</a></sup> The club had its period of greatest success in the middle of the 1970s when, under the <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captaincy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a>, it won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> three times in a row (1974–1976). Overall, Bayern has reached ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_Cup_and_UEFA_Champions_League_finals" title="List of European Cup and UEFA Champions League finals">European Cup/UEFA Champions League finals</a>, most recently winning their <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">fifth</a> title in <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">2013</a> as part of a continental <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">treble</a>. Bayern has also won one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a>, one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a>, one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a>, one <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cups</a>, making it <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_club_competition_winners" title="List of UEFA club competition winners">one of the most successful European clubs internationally</a>. Since the formation of the Bundesliga, Bayern has been the dominant club in German football with 26 titles and has won 8 of the last 12 titles. They have <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_football_derbies" title="Bavarian football derbies">traditional local rivalries</a> with <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">1860 Munich</a> and <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a>, as well as with <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> since the mid-1990s.</p>
<p>Since the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2005–06 FC Bayern Munich season">2005–06 season</a>, Bayern has played its home games at the <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a>. Previously the team had played at Munich's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Munich)" title="Olympic Stadium (Munich)">Olympiastadion</a> for 33 years. The team colours are red and white, and the team crest shows the white and blue <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Bavaria" title="Flag of Bavaria">flag of Bavaria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crestcolor_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-crestcolor-7">[7]</a></sup> In terms of <a href="/wiki/Deloitte_Football_Money_League" title="Deloitte Football Money League">revenue</a>, Bayern Munich is the biggest sports club in Germany and the third biggest football club in the world, generating €487.5 million for the 2013–14 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Bayern has over 270,000 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> There are more than 4,000 officially-registered fan clubs with over 314,000 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fan_Clubs_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fan_Clubs-10">[10]</a></sup> The club has other departments for <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a>, basketball, gymnastics, <a href="/wiki/Skittles_(sport)" title="Skittles (sport)">bowling</a>, table tennis and senior football with more than 1,100 active members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otherdepartments_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-otherdepartments-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>FC Bayern is ranked second in the current <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> <a href="/wiki/UEFA_coefficient#UEFA_team_ranking" title="UEFA coefficient">club coefficient rankings</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and fourth in <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Football_History_%26_Statistics" title="International Federation of Football History &amp; Statistics">IFFHS</a>'s latest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IFFHS#Current_ranking" title="IFFHS">IFFHS Club World Ranking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_FC_Bayern_Munich" title="History of FC Bayern Munich">History of FC Bayern Munich</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_.281900.E2.80.931965.29">Early years (1900–1965)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years (1900–1965)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fcn-fcb1901.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="194" data-file-width="350" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Fcn-fcb1901.jpg/220px-Fcn-fcb1901.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Fcn-fcb1901.jpg/330px-Fcn-fcb1901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/42/Fcn-fcb1901.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fcn-fcb1901.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first game of FC Bayern Munich against <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">Nürnberg</a> in 1901</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>FC Bayern Munich was founded by members of a Munich gymnastics club (MTV 1879). When a congregation of members of MTV 1879 decided on 27 February 1900 that the footballers of the club would not be allowed to join the <a href="/wiki/German_Football_Association" title="German Football Association">German Football Association</a> (DFB), 11 members of the football division left the congregation and on the same evening founded Fußball-Club Bayern München. Within a few months, Bayern achieved high-scoring victories against all local rivals, including a 15–0 win against FC Nordstern,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and reached the semi-finals of the 1900–01 <a href="/wiki/Southern_German_football_championship" title="Southern German football championship">South German championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcbbook1stch_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-fcbbook1stch-4">[4]</a></sup> In the following years, the club won some local trophies and in 1910–11 Bayern joined the newly founded "Kreisliga", the first regional Bavarian league. The club won this league in its first year, but did not win it again until the beginning of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in 1914, which halted all football activities in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory0045_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory0045-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the years after the war, Bayern won several regional competitions before winning its first South German championship in 1926, an achievement repeated two years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory0045_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory0045-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Its first national title was gained in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_football_championship_1932" title="German football championship 1932">1932</a>, when coach <a href="/wiki/Richard_Kohn" title="Richard Kohn">Richard "Little Dombi" Kohn</a> led the team to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_champions_(football)" title="German champions (football)">German championship</a> by defeating <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a> 2–0 in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory0045_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory0045-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The advent of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a> put an abrupt end to Bayern's development. Club president <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Landauer" title="Kurt Landauer">Kurt Landauer</a> and the coach, both of whom were Jewish, left the country. Many others in the club were also purged. Bayern was taunted as the "<a href="/wiki/Judenklub" title="Judenklub">Jew's club</a>", while local rival <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">1860 Munich</a> gained much support. Josef Sauter, who was inaugurated 1943, was the only NSDAP member as president. As some Bayern players greeted Landauer, who was watching a friendly in Switzerland lead to continued discrimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landauer_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-landauer-17">[17]</a></sup> Bayern was also affected by the ruling that football players had to be full amateurs again. In the following years, Bayern could not sustain its role of contender for the national title, achieving mid-table results in its regional league instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the war, Bayern became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Oberliga_S%C3%BCd_(1945%E2%80%9363)" title="Oberliga Süd (1945–63)">Oberliga Süd</a>, the southern conference of the German first division, which was split five ways at that time. Bayern struggled, hiring and firing 13 coaches between 1945 and 1963. Landauer returned from exile in 1947 and was once again appointed club president, the tenure lasted until 1951. He remains as the club's president with the longest accumulated tenure. Landauer has been deemed as inventor of Bayern as a professional club and his memory is e.g. being upheld by the Bayern <a href="/wiki/Ultra" title="Ultra">ultras</a> <i>Schickeria</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1955, the club was relegated but returned to the <i>Oberliga</i> in the following season and won the <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> for the first time, beating <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Fortuna Düsseldorf">Fortuna Düsseldorf</a> 1–0 in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal_1956%E2%80%9357#Final" title="DFB-Pokal 1956–57">final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory4667_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory4667-22">[22]</a></sup> The club struggled financially though, verging on bankruptcy at the end of the 1950s. Manufacturer Roland Endler provided the necessary funds and was rewarded with four years at the helm of the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1963, the Oberligas in Germany were consolidated into one national league, the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>. Five teams from the Oberliga South were admitted. Bayern finished third in that year's southern division, but another Munich team, 1860 Munich, had won the championship. As the DFB preferred not to include two teams from one city, Bayern was not chosen for the Bundesliga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nobl_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-nobl-6">[6]</a></sup> They gained promotion two years later, fielding a team with young talents like <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Gerd Müller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Maier" title="Sepp Maier">Sepp Maier</a> — who would later be collectively referred to as <i>the axis</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory4667_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory4667-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Golden_years_.281965.E2.80.931979.29">Golden years (1965–1979)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Golden years (1965–1979)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N1108-304,_Fu%C3%9Fball-Europapokalspiel,_Magdeburg_-_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="529" data-file-width="800" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N1108-304%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-Europapokalspiel%2C_Magdeburg_-_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N1108-304%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-Europapokalspiel%2C_Magdeburg_-_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N1108-304%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-Europapokalspiel%2C_Magdeburg_-_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N1108-304%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-Europapokalspiel%2C_Magdeburg_-_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N1108-304%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-Europapokalspiel%2C_Magdeburg_-_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N1108-304%2C_Fu%C3%9Fball-Europapokalspiel%2C_Magdeburg_-_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-N1108-304,_Fu%C3%9Fball-Europapokalspiel,_Magdeburg_-_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
FC Bayern Munich against 1. FC Magdeburg in 1974</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In their first Bundesliga <a href="/wiki/1965%E2%80%9366_Bundesliga" title="1965–66 Bundesliga">season</a>, Bayern finished third and also won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal_1965%E2%80%9366" title="DFB-Pokal 1965–66">DFB-Pokal</a>. This qualified them for the following year's <a href="/wiki/1966%E2%80%9367_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1966–67 European Cup Winners' Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a>, which they won in a dramatic <a href="/wiki/1967_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_Final" title="1967 European Cup Winners' Cup Final">final</a> against Scottish club <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Franz_Roth" title="Franz Roth">Franz Roth</a> scored the decider in a 1–0 <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)" title="Overtime (sports)">extra time</a> victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory4667_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory4667-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1967, Bayern retained the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal_1966%E2%80%9367" title="DFB-Pokal 1966–67">DFB-Pokal</a>, but slow overall progress saw <a href="/wiki/Branko_Zebec" title="Branko Zebec">Branko Zebec</a> take over as coach. He replaced Bayern's offensive style of play with a more disciplined approach, and in doing so achieved the first <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_Bundesliga" title="1968–69 Bundesliga">league</a> and <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_DFB-Pokal" title="1968–69 DFB-Pokal">cup</a> <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">double</a> in Bundesliga history in 1969. Bayern Munich are one of four German clubs to win the Bundesliga and DFB-Pokal in the same season along with <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/1._FC_K%C3%B6ln" title="1. FC Köln">1. FC Köln</a> and <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a>. Zebec used only 13 players throughout <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1968–69 FC Bayern Munich season">the season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Udo_Lattek" title="Udo Lattek">Udo Lattek</a> took charge in 1970. After winning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal_1970%E2%80%9371" title="DFB-Pokal 1970–71">DFB-Pokal</a> in <a href="/wiki/1970%E2%80%9371_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1970–71 FC Bayern Munich season">his first season</a>, Lattek led Bayern to their <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Bundesliga" title="1971–72 Bundesliga">third German championship</a>. The deciding match in the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1971–72 FC Bayern Munich season">1971–72</a> season against <a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04" title="FC Schalke 04">Schalke 04</a> was the first match in the new <a href="/wiki/Olympiastadion_(Munich)" title="Olympiastadion (Munich)">Olympiastadion</a>, and was also the first live televised match in Bundesliga history. Bayern beat Schalke 5–1 and thus claimed the title, also setting several records, including points gained and goals scored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Bayern also won the next two championships, but the zenith was their triumph in the <a href="/wiki/1974_European_Cup_Final" title="1974 European Cup Final">1974 European Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a>, which Bayern won 4–0 after a replay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory6876_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory6876-26">[26]</a></sup> This title – after winning the Cup Winners' trophy 1967 and two semi-finals (<a href="/wiki/1967%E2%80%9368_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1967–68 European Cup Winners' Cup">1968</a> and <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1971–72 European Cup Winners' Cup">1972</a>) in that competition – marked the club's breakthrough as a force on the international stage. During the following years, the team was unsuccessful domestically but defended their European title by defeating <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1975_European_Cup_Final" title="1975 European Cup Final">1975 European Cup Final</a> when Roth and Müller secured victory with late goals. "We came back into the game and scored two lucky goals, so in the end we were the winners but we were very, very lucky", stated Franz Beckenbauer. <a href="/wiki/Billy_Bremner" title="Billy Bremner">Billy Bremner</a> believed the French referee was "very suspicious". Leeds fans then rioted in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> and were banned from European football for three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unlucky_match_for_Leeds_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Unlucky_match_for_Leeds-27">[27]</a></sup> A year later in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/AS_Saint-%C3%89tienne" title="AS Saint-Étienne">Saint-Étienne</a> were <a href="/wiki/1976_European_Cup_Final" title="1976 European Cup Final">defeated</a> by another Roth goal and Bayern became the third club to win the trophy in three consecutive years. The final trophy won by Bayern in this era was the <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cup</a>, in which they defeated Brazilian club <a href="/wiki/Cruzeiro_Esporte_Clube" title="Cruzeiro Esporte Clube">Cruzeiro</a> over two legs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The rest of the decade was a time of change and saw no further titles for Bayern. In 1977, Franz Beckenbauer left for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Cosmos_(1971%E2%80%931985)" title="New York Cosmos (1971–1985)">New York Cosmos</a> and, in 1979, Sepp Maier and <a href="/wiki/Uli_Hoene%C3%9F" title="Uli Hoeneß">Uli Hoeneß</a> retired while Gerd Müller joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale_Strikers_(NASL)" title="Fort Lauderdale Strikers (NASL)">Fort Lauderdale Strikers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Bayern-luck" title="Bayern-luck">Bayerndusel</a></i> was coined during this period as an expression of either contempt or envy about the sometimes narrow and last-minute wins against other teams.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_FC_Breitnigge_to_FC_Hollywood_.281979.E2.80.931998.29">From FC Breitnigge to FC Hollywood (1979–1998)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: From FC Breitnigge to FC Hollywood (1979–1998)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1980s were a period of off-field turmoil for Bayern, with many changes in personnel and financial problems. On the field, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Breitner" title="Paul Breitner">Paul Breitner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karl-Heinz_Rummenigge" title="Karl-Heinz Rummenigge">Karl-Heinz Rummenigge</a>, termed <i>FC Breitnigge</i>, led the team to Bundesliga titles in <a href="/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_Bundesliga" title="1979–80 Bundesliga">1980</a> and <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Bundesliga" title="1980–81 Bundesliga">1981</a>. Apart from a DFB-Pokal win in <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_DFB-Pokal" title="1981–82 DFB-Pokal">1982</a>, two relatively unsuccessful seasons followed, after which Breitner retired and former coach Udo Lattek returned. Bayern won the DFB-Pokal in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal_1983%E2%80%9384" title="DFB-Pokal 1983–84">1984</a> and went on to win five Bundesliga championships in six seasons, including a <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">double</a> in <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1985–86 FC Bayern Munich season">1986</a>. European success, however, was elusive during the decade; Bayern managed to claim the runners-up spot in the European Cup in <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_European_Cup" title="1981–82 European Cup">1982</a> and <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_European_Cup" title="1986–87 European Cup">1987</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jupp_Heynckes" title="Jupp Heynckes">Jupp Heynckes</a> was hired as coach in 1987, but after two consecutive championships in <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Bundesliga" title="1988–89 Bundesliga">1988–89</a> and <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Bundesliga" title="1989–90 Bundesliga">1989–90</a>, Bayern's form dipped. After finishing second in <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Bundesliga" title="1990–91 Bundesliga">1990–91</a>, the club finished just five points above the relegation places in <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Bundesliga" title="1991–92 Bundesliga">1991–92</a>. In <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1993–94 FC Bayern Munich season">1993–94</a>, Bayern was eliminated in the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_UEFA_Cup" title="1993–94 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> second round to <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> side <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>, who remain the only English club to beat Bayern at the Olympiastadion. Success returned when Franz Beckenbauer took over for the second half of the 1993–94 season, winning the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Bundesliga" title="1993–94 Bundesliga">championship</a> again after a four-year gap. Beckenbauer was then appointed club president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>His successors as coach, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Trapattoni" title="Giovanni Trapattoni">Giovanni Trapattoni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Otto_Rehhagel" title="Otto Rehhagel">Otto Rehhagel</a>, both finished trophyless after a season, not meeting the club's high expectations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory9199_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory9199-32">[32]</a></sup> During this time, Bayern's players frequently appeared in the gossip pages of the press rather than the sports pages, resulting in the nickname <i>FC Hollywood</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Franz Beckenbauer briefly returned at the end of the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Bundesliga" title="1995–96 Bundesliga">1995–96</a> season as caretaker coach and led his team to victory in the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_UEFA_Cup" title="1995–96 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>, beating <a href="/wiki/FC_Girondins_de_Bordeaux" title="FC Girondins de Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1996_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="1996 UEFA Cup Final">final</a>. For the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1996–97 FC Bayern Munich season">1996–97 season</a>, Trapattoni returned to win <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Bundesliga" title="1996–97 Bundesliga">the championship</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1997–98 FC Bayern Munich season">following season</a>, Bayern lost <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Bundesliga" title="1997–98 Bundesliga">the title</a> to newly promoted <a href="/wiki/1._FC_Kaiserslautern" title="1. FC Kaiserslautern">1. FC Kaiserslautern</a> and Trapattoni had to take his leave for the second time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewed_international_success_.281998.E2.80.93present.29">Renewed international success (1998–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Renewed international success (1998–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Allianz_Arena_Pahu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="782" data-file-width="1508" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Allianz_Arena_Pahu.jpg/350px-Allianz_Arena_Pahu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Allianz_Arena_Pahu.jpg/525px-Allianz_Arena_Pahu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Allianz_Arena_Pahu.jpg/700px-Allianz_Arena_Pahu.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Allianz_Arena_Pahu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Opened in 2005: the <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a>, one of the world's most <a href="/wiki/Stadium#The_modern_stadium" title="Stadium">modern football stadiums</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After his success at Borussia Dortmund, Bayern were coached by <a href="/wiki/Ottmar_Hitzfeld" title="Ottmar Hitzfeld">Ottmar Hitzfeld</a> from 1998 to 2004. In Hitzfeld's <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1998–99 FC Bayern Munich season">first season</a>, Bayern won the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_Bundesliga" title="1998–99 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> and came close to winning the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1998–99 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>, losing 2–1 to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> into injury time after leading for most of the <a href="/wiki/1999_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1999 UEFA Champions League Final">match</a>. The following year, in <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1999–2000 FC Bayern Munich season">the club's centenary season</a>, Bayern won the third <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Bundesliga" title="1999–2000 Bundesliga">league</a> and <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_DFB-Pokal" title="1999–2000 DFB-Pokal">cup</a> <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">double</a> in its history. A third consecutive <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Bundesliga" title="2000–01 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> title followed in <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2000–01 FC Bayern Munich season">2001</a>, won with a stoppage time goal on the final day of the league season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Days later, Bayern won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> for the fourth time after a 25-year gap, defeating <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(association_football)" title="Penalty shootout (association football)">penalties</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2001–02 FC Bayern Munich season">2001–02 season</a> began with a win in the <a href="/wiki/2001_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2001 Intercontinental Cup">Intercontinental Cup</a>, but ended trophyless otherwise. In <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2002–03 FC Bayern Munich season">2002–03</a>, Bayern won their fourth double, leading the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Bundesliga" title="2002–03 Bundesliga">league</a> by a record margin of 16 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Hitzfeld's reign ended in 2004, with Bayern underperforming, including defeat by second division <a href="/wiki/Alemannia_Aachen" title="Alemannia Aachen">Alemannia Aachen</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_DFB-Pokal" title="2003–04 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Felix_Magath" title="Felix Magath">Felix Magath</a> took over and led Bayern to two consecutive <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">doubles</a>. Prior to the start of the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Bundesliga" title="2005–06 Bundesliga">2005–06 season</a>, Bayern moved from the Olympiastadion to the new <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a>, which the club shares with 1860 Munich. On the field, their performance in <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Bundesliga" title="2006–07 Bundesliga">2006–07</a> was erratic. Trailing in the league and having lost to Alemannia Aachen in the cup yet again, coach Magath was sacked shortly after the winter break.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hitzfeld returned as trainer in January 2007, but Bayern finished the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Bundesliga" title="2006–07 Bundesliga">2006–07 season</a> in fourth position, thus failing to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2007–08 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> for the first time in more than a decade. Additional losses in the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_DFB-Pokal" title="2006–07 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_DFB-Ligapokal" title="2007 DFB-Ligapokal">DFB-Ligapokal</a> left the club with no honours for the season.</p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2007–08 FC Bayern Munich season">2007–08 season</a>, Bayern made drastic squad changes to help rebuild. They signed a total of eight new players and sold, released or loaned out nine of their players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Among new signings were <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> stars such as <a href="/wiki/Franck_Rib%C3%A9ry" title="Franck Ribéry">Franck Ribéry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Klose" title="Miroslav Klose">Miroslav Klose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luca_Toni" title="Luca Toni">Luca Toni</a>. Bayern went on to win the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Bundesliga" title="2007–08 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>, being on top of the standings on every single week of play, and the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_DFB-Pokal" title="2007–08 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> against Borussia Dortmund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fussballdaten_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-fussballdaten-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 January 2008, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klinsmann" title="Jürgen Klinsmann">Jürgen Klinsmann</a> was named as Hitzfeld's successor, taking charge on 1 July 2008 after signing a two-year contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mark25787_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-mark25787-41">[41]</a></sup> Bayern Munich lost the <a href="/wiki/DFL-Supercup" title="DFL-Supercup">DFL-Supercup</a> 1–2 against Borussia Dortmund in 2008 then was eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a> in the quarter-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_DFB-Pokal" title="2008–09 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2008–09 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> Bayern also reached the quarter-finals after winning Group F and defeating <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Clube_de_Portugal" title="Sporting Clube de Portugal">Sporting CP</a> in the first knockout round, achieving a Champions League record aggregate of 12–1. On 27 April, two days after a home defeat against Schalke 04 which saw Bayern drop to the third place in the table, Klinsmann was fired. Former trainer Jupp Heynckes was named as caretaker until the end of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-klinsmannfired_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-klinsmannfired-42">[42]</a></sup> Bayern eventually finished second, thus qualifying directly for the Champions League in 2009–10.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bayern_munich_bayer_leverkusen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Bayern_munich_bayer_leverkusen.jpg/220px-Bayern_munich_bayer_leverkusen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Bayern_munich_bayer_leverkusen.jpg/330px-Bayern_munich_bayer_leverkusen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Bayern_munich_bayer_leverkusen.jpg/440px-Bayern_munich_bayer_leverkusen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bayern_munich_bayer_leverkusen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bayern Munich playing against <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> in September 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bayern then signed <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2009–10 FC Bayern Munich season">2009–10 season</a>. Multi-million signings of <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B3mez" title="Mario Gómez">Mario Gómez</a> also followed in a bid to return Bayern to the top of the European scene. On 8 May 2010, Bayern Munich won the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Bundesliga" title="2009–10 Bundesliga">2009–10 Bundesliga</a> after a 3–1 win at <a href="/wiki/Hertha_BSC" title="Hertha BSC">Hertha BSC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Bayern then won the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_DFB-Pokal" title="2009–10 DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a> on 15 May 2010 to secure the domestic double.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Bayern also reached the <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2010 UEFA Champions League Final">2010 Champions League final</a>, but were beaten 2–0 by <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a>, failing to become the first German club to complete <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">the treble</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2010–11 FC Bayern Munich season">2010–11 season</a>, Bayern were eliminated in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2010–11 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> knockout phase by Inter Milan on the <a href="/wiki/Away_goals_rule" title="Away goals rule">away goals rule</a> and finished third in the Bundesliga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Van Gaal was fired by Bayern in April 2011.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2011–12 FC Bayern Munich season">2011–12 season</a>, Heynckes returned to coach Bayern for a second permanent spell but the team was to end the season without a trophy for the second season running. Domestically they finished second in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Bundesliga" title="2011–12 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> and lost the <a href="/wiki/2012_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2012 DFB-Pokal Final">DFB-Pokal final</a> 2–5, both times finishing runner-up to Borussia Dortmund. They also reached the <a href="/wiki/2012_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2012 UEFA Champions League Final">final of the Champions League</a> in their home stadium, but lost to <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> on penalties (3–4) in what was only the club's second defeat to an English team in Munich, and their first at the Allianz Arena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2012–13 FC Bayern Munich season">2012–13 season</a>, Bayern won the <a href="/wiki/2012_DFL-Supercup" title="2012 DFL-Supercup">2012 DFL-Supercup</a> 2–1 against rivals Borussia Dortmund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Bayern became the first team in history to win their first eight matches in the Bundesliga after their 5–0 away win to <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Fortuna Düsseldorf">Fortuna Düsseldorf</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> On 6 April 2013, Bayern won the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Bundesliga" title="2012–13 Bundesliga">2012–13 Bundesliga</a> after a 1–0 win at <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a> with six games left, setting a new record for being the earliest ever Bundesliga winners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga#Club_records" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga records</a> set by Bayern in the 2012–13 season include most points in a season (91), highest league winning points margin (25), most wins in a season (29) and fewest goals conceded in a season (18). Bayern also equaled the record for fewest defeats in a season, losing once, to Bayer Leverkusen. Bayern also reached the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League final</a> for the third time in four seasons, winning the club's fifth <a href="/wiki/European_Champion_Clubs%27_Cup" title="European Champion Clubs' Cup">European Cup</a> with a 2–1 defeat of domestic rivals Borussia Dortmund at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> On 1 June 2013, Bayern beat <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a> 3–2 in the <a href="/wiki/2013_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2013 DFB-Pokal Final">2013 DFB-Pokal final</a> to become the first German club in men's football to complete the treble; Bayern had missed out on trebles in 1999 and 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 July 2013, <a href="/wiki/Pep_Guardiola" title="Pep Guardiola">Pep Guardiola</a> took over as manager ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2013–14 FC Bayern Munich season">2013–14 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Bayern also completed the signing of <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B6tze" title="Mario Götze">Mario Götze</a> from Borussia Dortmund for €37 million, who became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_footballers#Highest_fees" title="List of most expensive footballers">most expensive</a> German player in history (this was later surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Mesut_%C3%96zil" title="Mesut Özil">Mesut Özil</a>'s transfer from <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> to <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> for €50 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> On 24 July 2013, it was reported that Bayern had become the first German club with over 200,000 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-membersjuly13_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-membersjuly13-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> On 27 July 2013, Bayern Munich lost against rivals Borussia Dortmund 2–4 in the <a href="/wiki/2013_DFL-Supercup" title="2013 DFL-Supercup">2013 DFL-Supercup</a> at <a href="/wiki/Westfalenstadion" title="Westfalenstadion">Signal Iduna Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> On 30 August 2013, Bayern won the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2013 UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a> against Chelsea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UEFA_1942071_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-UEFA_1942071-60">[60]</a></sup> On 9 November 2013, Bayern set a new <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga#Records" title="Bundesliga">record</a> for most successive Bundesliga matches without defeat, breaking <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a>'s 30-year-old record of 36 matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> This record was eventually extended to 53 matches, before Bayern lost 1–0 to <a href="/wiki/FC_Augsburg" title="FC Augsburg">FC Augsburg</a> in April 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> On 27 November 2013, Bayern became the first team to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League_records_and_statistics#Consecutive_wins" title="UEFA Champions League records and statistics">win ten consecutive Champions League matches</a> with a 3–1 away victory over <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On 21 December 2013, Bayern beat <a href="/wiki/Raja_Casablanca" title="Raja Casablanca">Raja Casablanca</a> 2–0 at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_de_Marrakech" title="Stade de Marrakech">Stade de Marrakech</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Club World Cup">2013 FIFA Club World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>After almost a year of investigations against Uli Hoeneß, Bayern's former player, former long time general manager, and president at the time, he was convicted of tax evasion on 13 March 2014. Hoeneß resigned as president the next day, and Karl Hopfner was elected president on 2 May. Just days after Hoeneß conviction, on 25 March, Bayern won their 24th <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Bundesliga" title="2013–14 Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> title by beating Hertha BSC 3–1 at the <a href="/wiki/Olympiastadion_(Berlin)" title="Olympiastadion (Berlin)">Olympiastadion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>. With seven matches remaining in the season, it was the earliest the championship had been won in Bundesliga history, breaking the record Bayern had set in the previous season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> At the end of the season Bayern beat Borussia Dortmund 2–0 in the <a href="/wiki/2014_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2014 DFB-Pokal Final">2014 DFB-Pokal Final</a> to give the club the tenth league and cup double in its history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2014–15 FC Bayern Munich season">2014–15</a>, Bayern defended their <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Bundesliga" title="2015–16 Bundesliga">league</a> title, and, the following season, won an 11th double, including a record fourth consecutive Bundesliga title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> At the end of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2015–16 FC Bayern Munich season">2015–16</a> season, Guardiola left Bayern to take over as manager of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ancelotti" title="Carlo Ancelotti">Carlo Ancelotti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours">Colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the original club constitution, Bayern's colours were named as white and blue, but the club played in white shirts with black shorts until 1905, when Bayern joined MSC. MSC decreed that the footballers would have to play in red shorts. Also the younger players were called red-shorts, which was meant as an insult.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcbbook1stch_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-fcbbook1stch-4">[4]</a></sup> For most of the club's early history, Bayern had primarily worn white and maroon home kits. In <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1968–69 FC Bayern Munich season">1968–69 season</a>, Bayern changed to red and blue striped shirts, with blue shorts and socks. Between 1969 and 1973, the team wore a home strip of red and white striped shirts with either red or white shorts and red socks. In the <a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1973–74 FC Bayern Munich season">1973–74 season</a>, the team switched to an all white kit featuring single vertical red and blue stripes on the shirt. From 1974 onwards, Bayern have mostly worn an all red home kit, with white trim. Bayern revived the red and blue striped colour scheme between 1995 and 1997. In 1997, blue was the dominant colour for the first time when Adidas released an all <a href="/wiki/Navy_blue" title="Navy blue">navy blue</a> home kit with a red chest band. In 1999, Bayern returned to a predominantly red kit, which featured blue sleeves, and in 2000 the club released a traditional all red kit with white trim to be worn for Champions League matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crestcolor_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-crestcolor-7">[7]</a></sup> Bayern also wore a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burgundy_(colour)" title="Burgundy (colour)">Rotwein</a></i> coloured home kits in Bundesliga matches between 2001 and 2003, and during the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2006–07 UEFA Champions League">2006–07 Champions League</a> campaign, in reference to their first choice colours prior to the late 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club's away kit has had a wide range of colours over the years, including white, black, blue, and gold-green. Bayern also features a distinct international kit. During the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2013–14 FC Bayern Munich season">2013–14 season</a>, Bayern have used an all red home kit with a <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Bavaria" title="Flag of Bavaria">Bavarian flag</a> diamond watermark pattern, a <i><a href="/wiki/Lederhosen" title="Lederhosen">Lederhosen</a></i> inspired white and black <i><a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">Oktoberfest</a></i> away kit, and an all navy blue international kit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1980s and 1990s, Bayern used a special away kit when playing at <a href="/wiki/1._FC_Kaiserslautern" title="1. FC Kaiserslautern">1. FC Kaiserslautern</a>, representing the <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazilian</a> colours blue and yellow, a <a href="/wiki/Superstition" title="Superstition">superstition</a> borne from the fact that the club found it hard to win there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_kits">Historical kits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Historical kits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crest">Crest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Crest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bayern's crest has changed several times. Originally it consisted of the stylised letters F, C, B, M, which were woven into one symbol. The original crest was blue. The colours of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> were included for the first time in 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crestcolor_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-crestcolor-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The modern version of the crest has changed from the 1954 version in several steps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crestcolor_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-crestcolor-7">[7]</a></sup> While the crest consisted of a single colour only for most of the time, namely blue or red, the current (2008) crest is blue, red, and white. It has the colours of Bavaria in its centre and FC Bayern München is written in white on a red ring enclosing the Bavarian colours.</p>
