<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadiums">Stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Model_of_stadium_at_Leopoldstrasse.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2576" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Model_of_stadium_at_Leopoldstrasse.JPG/220px-Model_of_stadium_at_Leopoldstrasse.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Model_of_stadium_at_Leopoldstrasse.JPG/330px-Model_of_stadium_at_Leopoldstrasse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Model_of_stadium_at_Leopoldstrasse.JPG/440px-Model_of_stadium_at_Leopoldstrasse.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Model_of_stadium_at_Leopoldstrasse.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Model of Bayern's first stadium, their home from 1906 to 1924</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bayern played its first training games at the Schyrenplatz in the centre of <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. The first official games were held on the <a href="/wiki/Theresienwiese" title="Theresienwiese">Theresienwiese</a>. In 1901, Bayern moved to a field of its own, located in <a href="/wiki/Schwabing" title="Schwabing">Schwabing</a> at the Clemensstraße. After joining the Münchner Sport-Club (MSC) in 1906, Bayern moved in May 1907 to MSC's ground at the Leopoldstraße.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> As the crowds gathering for Bayern's home games increased at the beginning of the 1920s, Bayern had to switch to various other premises in Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 1925, Bayern shared the <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnwalder_Stadion" title="Grünwalder Stadion">Grünwalder Stadion</a> with <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">1860 Munich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Until World War II, the stadium was owned by 1860 Munich, and is still colloquially known as <i>Sechz'ger</i> ("Sixties") Stadium. It was destroyed during the war, and efforts to rebuild it resulted in a patchwork. Bayern's record crowd at the Grünwalder Stadion is reported as more than 50,000 in the home game against <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1961%E2%80%9362_Oberliga" title="1961–62 Oberliga">1961–62</a> season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> era the stadium had a maximum capacity of 44,000 which was reached on several occasions, but the capacity has since been reduced to 21,272. As was the case at most of this period's stadiums, the vast majority of the stadium was given over to terracing. Today the second teams of both clubs play in the stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olympiastadion_Muenchen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="661" data-file-width="974" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Olympiastadion_Muenchen.jpg/220px-Olympiastadion_Muenchen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Olympiastadion_Muenchen.jpg/330px-Olympiastadion_Muenchen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Olympiastadion_Muenchen.jpg/440px-Olympiastadion_Muenchen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Olympiastadion_Muenchen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Munich)" title="Olympic Stadium (Munich)">Olympiastadion</a>, home of Bayern Munich from 1972 to 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Summer Olympics</a> the city of Munich built the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Munich)" title="Olympic Stadium (Munich)">Olympiastadion</a>. The stadium, renowned for its architecture,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> was inaugurated in the last Bundesliga match of the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Bundesliga" title="1971–72 Bundesliga">1971–72</a> season. The match drew a capacity crowd of 79,000, a total which was reached again on numerous occasions. The stadium was, in its early days, considered to be one of the foremost stadia in the world and played host to numerous major finals, such as that of <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In the following years the stadium underwent several modifications, such as an increase in seating space from approximately 50% to ca. 66% <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Eventually the stadium had a capacity of 63,000 for national matches, and 59,000 for international occasions such as European Cup competitions. Many people, however, began to feel that the stadium was too cold in winter, with half the audience exposed to the weather due to lack of cover. A further complaint was the distance between the spectators and the pitch, the stadium betraying its track and field heritage. Modification of the stadium proved impossible as the architect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G%C3%BCnther_Behnisch" title="Günther Behnisch">Günther Behnisch</a> vetoed major modifications of the stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diebayern_allianzarena_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-diebayern_allianzarena-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1786" data-file-width="5000" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/220px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/330px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/440px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
For Bayern home games, the <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a> is lit in red.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After much discussion, the city of Munich, the state of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, Bayern Munich and <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">1860 Munich</a> jointly decided at the end of 2000 to build a new stadium. While Bayern had wanted a purpose-built football stadium for several years, the awarding of the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a> to Germany stimulated the discussion as the Olympiastadion no longer met the <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> criteria to host a World Cup game. Located on the northern outskirts of Munich, the <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a> has been in use since the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Bundesliga" title="2005–06 Bundesliga">2005–06</a> season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diebayern_allianzarena_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-diebayern_allianzarena-80">[80]</a></sup> Its initial capacity of 66,000 fully covered seats has since been increased for matches on national level to 69,901 by transforming 3,000 seats to terracing in a 2:1 ratio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Since August 2012, 2,000 more seats were added in the last row of the top tier increasing the capacity to 71,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> In January 2015, a proposal to increase the capacity was approved by the city council so now Allianz Arena has a capacity of 75,000 (70,000 in Champions League).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most prominent feature of the stadium is the translucent outer layer, which can be illuminated in different colours for impressive effects. Usually, red lighting is used for Bayern home games, blue for <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">1860 Munich</a> games and white for <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">German national team</a> home games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2012, Bayern opened a museum about its history, FC Bayern Erlebniswelt, inside the Allianz Arena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_Fanshop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="2300" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_Fanshop.jpg/220px-FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_Fanshop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_Fanshop.jpg/330px-FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_Fanshop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_Fanshop.jpg/440px-FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_Fanshop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_Fanshop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Fan shop at Bräuhausstraße in Munich.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bayern considers itself a national club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The club had 3,202 fanclubs with total 231,197 members in 2012, making it the club with the largest number of organised supporters in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Owing partly to the club having supporters all over the country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fan_Clubs_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fan_Clubs-10">[10]</a></sup> all of Bayern's away games have been sold out in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weltfussball_attendance_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-weltfussball_attendance-88">[88]</a></sup> Their following is mainly recruited from the aspiring middle class and regional Bavaria.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Despite a large proportion of their supporters having to travel more than 200 km (ca. 120 miles) regularly,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> the club's home matches in the <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a> have almost always been sold out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weltfussball_attendance_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-weltfussball_attendance-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allianzarena_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-allianzarena-90">[90]</a></sup> According to a study by Sport+Markt Bayern is the fifth-most popular football club in Europe with 20.7 million supporters, and the most popular football club in Germany with 10 million supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bayern Munich is also renowned for its well-organised <a href="/wiki/Ultras" title="Ultras">ultra</a> scene. The most prominent groups are the <i>Schickeria München</i>, the <i>Inferno Bavaria</i>, the <i>Red Munichs '89</i>, the <i>Südkurve '73</i>, the <i>Munichmaniacs 1996</i>, the <i>Red Angels</i>, and the <i>Red Sharks</i>. The ultras scene of Bayern Munch has been recognized for certain groups taking stance against right-wing extremism, racism and homophobia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> and in 2014 the group Schickeria München received the Julius Hirsch Award by the DFB for its commitment against antisemitism and discrimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stern_des_S%C3%BCdens" title="Stern des Südens">Stern des Südens</a> is the song which fans sing at FCB home games. In the 1990s they also used to sing <i>FC Bayern, Forever Number One</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club also has quite a number of high-profile supporters, among them <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boris_Becker" title="Boris Becker">Boris Becker</a>, retired German tennis player, <a href="/wiki/Wladimir_Klitschko" title="Wladimir Klitschko">Wladimir Klitschko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> boxer, <a href="/wiki/Horst_Seehofer" title="Horst Seehofer">Horst Seehofer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Stoiber" title="Edmund Stoiber">Edmund Stoiber</a>, former <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ministers-President_of_Bavaria" title="List of Ministers-President of Bavaria">Minister-President</a> of Bavaria, to name just a few.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bayernfans_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bayernfans-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_football_derbies" title="Bavarian football derbies">Bavarian football derbies</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1836" data-file-width="3264" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/220px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/330px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/440px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bayern Munich won 2–1 against rivals <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">2013 UEFA Champions League</a> on 25 May 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bayern Munich has a rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Bayern and Dortmund have competed against each other for many Bundesliga titles. Bayern and Dortmund have played against each other in the DFB-Pokal final in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_DFB-Pokal" title="2007–08 DFB-Pokal">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_DFB-Pokal" title="2011–12 DFB-Pokal">2012</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2014_DFB-Pokal_Final" title="2014 DFB-Pokal Final">2014</a>. The 2–5 loss against Dortmund in the 2012 DFB-Pokal final was Bayern's worst ever loss in a final. Bayern and Dortmund have also played against each other in the DFL-Supercup in <a href="/wiki/1989_DFB-Supercup" title="1989 DFB-Supercup">1989</a>, 2008, <a href="/wiki/2012_DFL-Supercup" title="2012 DFL-Supercup">2012</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_DFL-Supercup" title="2013 DFL-Supercup">2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_DFL-Supercup" title="2014 DFL-Supercup">2014</a>. The height of the rivalry was when Bayern defeated Dortmund, 2–1 in the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">final</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">2013 UEFA Champions League</a>.</p>
<p>Bayern is one of three professional football clubs in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. Bayern's main local rival is <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">1860 Munich</a>, who were the more successful club in the 1960s, winning a cup and a championship. In the 1970s and 1980s, 1860 Munich moved between the first and the third division, but lately have settled in the <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">second division</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Munich_derby" title="Munich derby">Munich derby</a> is still a much anticipated event, getting a lot of extra attention from supporters of both clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> 1860 Munich is considered more working-class, and therefore suffers from a diminishing fan base in a city where the manufacturing sector is declining.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Bayern is considered the establishment club,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsv1860_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-tsv1860-104">[104]</a></sup> which is reflected by many board members being business leaders<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (January 2013)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:FC_Bayern_Munich#Dubious" title="Talk:FC Bayern Munich">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> and including the former Bavarian minister president, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Stoiber" title="Edmund Stoiber">Edmund Stoiber</a>. Despite the rivalry, Bayern has repeatedly supported 1860 in times of financial disarray.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsv1860_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-tsv1860-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the 1920s, <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a> has been Bayern's main and traditional<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bavarian_Derby_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bavarian_Derby-105">[105]</a></sup> rival in Bavaria. <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Lahm" title="Philipp Lahm">Philipp Lahm</a> said that playing Nürnberg is "always special" and is a "heated atmosphere".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bavarian_Derby_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bavarian_Derby-105">[105]</a></sup> Both clubs played in the same league in the mid-1920s, but in the 1920s and 1930s, Nürnberg was far more successful, winning five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_football_champions" title="German football champions">championships</a> in the 1920s, making the club Germany's record champion. Bayern took over the title more than sixty years later, when they won their tenth championship in <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Bundesliga" title="1986–87 Bundesliga">1987</a>, thereby surpassing the number of championships won by Nürnberg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bavarian_Derby_105-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bavarian_Derby-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The duel between Bayern and Nürnberg is often referred to as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bavarian_football_derbys#The_Bavarian_derby" title="Bavarian football derbys">Bavarian Derby</a>.</p>
<p>Bayern also enjoys a strong rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/1._FC_Kaiserslautern" title="1. FC Kaiserslautern">1. FC Kaiserslautern</a>, originating in parts from a game in 1973, when Bayern lost 7–4 after leading 4–1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> but also from the two clubs competing for German championship honours at various times in the Bundesliga as well as the city of <a href="/wiki/Kaiserslautern" title="Kaiserslautern">Kaiserslautern</a> together with the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Palatinate_(region)" title="Palatinate (region)">Palatinate</a> having been part of Bavaria until a plebiscite after the end of the Second World War.</p>
<p>Since the 1970s, Bayern's main rivals have been the clubs who put up the strongest fight against its national dominance. In the 1970s this was <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory6876_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory6876-26">[26]</a></sup> in the 1980s the category expanded to include <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a>. In the 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory0003_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory0003-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> emerged as the most ardent opponents. Recently <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04" title="FC Schalke 04">Schalke</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> and Werder Bremen have been the main challengers in the Bundesliga.</p>
<p>Amongst Bayern's chief European rivals are <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> due to many classic wins, draws and losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayernhistory0003_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-bayernhistory0003-109">[109]</a></sup> Real Madrid versus Bayern is the match that has historically been played most often in the Champions League with 14 matches and the European Cup with 19 matches. Real's biggest loss at home in the Champions League came at the hands of Bayern on 29 February 2000 (2–4).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Due to Bayern being traditionally hard to beat for Madrid, Madrid supporters often refer to Bayern as the "<i>Bestia negra</i>" ("Black Beast"). Despite the number of duels, Bayern and Real have never met in the final of a Champions League or European Cup.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_finance">Organization and finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Organization and finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franz_Beckenbauer_2006_06_17.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="846" data-file-width="743" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Franz_Beckenbauer_2006_06_17.jpg/170px-Franz_Beckenbauer_2006_06_17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Franz_Beckenbauer_2006_06_17.jpg/255px-Franz_Beckenbauer_2006_06_17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Franz_Beckenbauer_2006_06_17.jpg/340px-Franz_Beckenbauer_2006_06_17.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Franz_Beckenbauer_2006_06_17.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bayern's former president from 1994 to 2009 and former player <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Most_valuable_sports_teams" title="Most valuable sports teams">Most valuable sports teams</a></div>
<p>Bayern is led mostly by former club players. Since 2 May 2014, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Hopfner" title="Karl Hopfner">Karl Hopfner</a> serves as the club's president, following <a href="/wiki/Uli_Hoene%C3%9F" title="Uli Hoeneß">Uli Hoeneß</a> who had been in office from 2009 to 2014; Hoeneß had resigned after being convicted of tax fraud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uli_Hoeness_resigns_as_Bayern_Munich_president_after_court_case_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Uli_Hoeness_resigns_as_Bayern_Munich_president_after_court_case-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karl-Heinz_Rummenigge" title="Karl-Heinz Rummenigge">Karl-Heinz Rummenigge</a> is the chairman of the executive board of the AG.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CompanyInfo_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-CompanyInfo-117">[117]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Supervisory_board" title="Supervisory board">supervisory board</a> of nine consists mostly of managers of big German corporations. Besides the club's president and the board's chairman Karl Hopfner, they are <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hainer" title="Herbert Hainer">Herbert Hainer</a> (Adidas), <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Stadler" title="Rupert Stadler">Rupert Stadler</a> (Audi), Werner Zedelius (Allianz), <a href="/wiki/Timotheus_H%C3%B6ttges" title="Timotheus Höttges">Timotheus Höttges</a> (Deutsche Telekom), Rudolf Schels, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Stoiber" title="Edmund Stoiber">Edmund Stoiber</a>, Theodor Weimer (UniCredit Bank), and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Winterkorn" title="Martin Winterkorn">Martin Winterkorn</a> (Volkswagen).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-supervisory_board_members_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-supervisory_board_members-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>Professional football at Bayern is run by the spin-off organization <i>FC Bayern München AG</i>. <i>AG</i> is short for <i><a href="/wiki/Aktiengesellschaft" title="Aktiengesellschaft">Aktiengesellschaft</a></i>, and Bayern is run like a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_stock_company" title="Joint stock company">joint stock company</a>, a company whose stock are not listed on the public stock exchange, but is privately owned. 75% of <i>FC Bayern München AG</i> is owned by the club, the <i>FC Bayern München e. V.</i> (<i>e. V.</i> is short for <i><a href="/wiki/Eingetragener_Verein" title="Eingetragener Verein">Eingetragener Verein</a></i>, which translates into "Registered Club"). Three Germany-based corporations, the sports goods manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>, the automobile company <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a> and the financial services group <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a> each hold 8.33% of the shares, 25% in total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CompanyInfo_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-CompanyInfo-117">[117]</a></sup> Adidas acquired its shares in 2002 for €77 million. The money was designated to help finance the <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> In 2009 Audi paid €90 million for their share. The capital was reportedly going to be used to repay the loan for the Allianz Arena quicker than originally planned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200809summary_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-200809summary-121">[121]</a></sup> And in early 2014, Allianz became the fourth stakeholder of the company acquiring theirs share for €110 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Bayern's other sports departments are run by the club.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Testspiel_gegen_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_03.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1292" data-file-width="2477" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Testspiel_gegen_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_03.JPG/220px-Testspiel_gegen_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_03.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Testspiel_gegen_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_03.JPG/330px-Testspiel_gegen_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Testspiel_gegen_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_03.JPG/440px-Testspiel_gegen_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_03.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Testspiel_gegen_FC_Bayern_M%C3%BCnchen_03.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bayern Munich team bus provided by their sponsor <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bayern's main advertising partner and current holder of the jersey rights is <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SponsorsSuppliers_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-SponsorsSuppliers-123">[123]</a></sup> The main supplier of the club is <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SponsorsSuppliers_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-SponsorsSuppliers-123">[123]</a></sup> The premium partners include <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a>, <a href="/wiki/HypoVereinsbank" title="HypoVereinsbank">HypoVereinsbank</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imtech" title="Imtech">Imtech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paulaner_Brewery" title="Paulaner Brewery">Paulaner Brewery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DHL" title="DHL">DHL</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yingli_Solar" title="Yingli Solar">Yingli Solar</a>. Classic sponsors include <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siemens_AG" title="Siemens AG">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hublot" title="Hublot">Hublot</a>, Henkel, Flyeralarm, Nestle Schoeller, Adelholzener,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fitness_First" title="Fitness First">Fitness First</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schaeffler_Group" title="Schaeffler Group">Schaeffler Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/S.Oliver" title="S.Oliver">s.Oliver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viagogo" title="Viagogo">Viagogo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trentino-Alto_Adige/S%C3%BCdtirol" title="Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol">Trentino</a>, Thomas Sabo and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Starwood_Hotels_and_Resorts_Worldwide" title="Starwood Hotels and Resorts Worldwide">Starwood Hotels and Resorts</a>. Food sponsors include Albi, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BiFi_(snack)" title="BiFi (snack)">BiFi</a>, Ehrmann and MF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SponsorsSuppliers_123-2"><a href="#cite_note-SponsorsSuppliers-123">[123]</a></sup> In previous years the jersey rights were held by Adidas<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> (1974–78), <a href="/wiki/Magirus" title="Magirus">Magirus Deutz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> (trucks / 1978–84), <a href="/wiki/Commodore_International" title="Commodore International">Commodore</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> (computers / 1984–89) and <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> (cars / 1989–2002).</p>
<p>Bayern is an exception in professional, international football, having generated profits in nine of the last ten seasons. Other clubs often report losses, realizing transfers via loans, whereas Bayern always uses <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Current_assets" title="Current assets">current assets</a>. Also Bayern differs from other European top clubs in their income composition. While other clubs derive more than 35% of their revenues from broadcasting right, Bayern earn only 22% of their revenues that way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> This is often accounted for by Bayern not marketing their broadcasting right themselves.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Instead the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Fu%C3%9Fball_Liga" title="Deutsche Fußball Liga">Deutsche Fußball Liga</a> negotiates broadcasting rights for the whole Bundesliga.</p>
<p>In 2011–12, Bayern reported revenues of €373.4 million, marking the eighth consecutive time that Bayern has topped their previous record earnings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201112summary_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-201112summary-130">[130]</a></sup> According to the 2013 edition of <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>'s annual <a href="/wiki/Deloitte_Football_Money_League" title="Deloitte Football Money League">Football Money League</a>, Bayern was the fourth richest club in the world in 2012, generating revenues of €368.4 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>While other European clubs have mainly marketed to international audiences, Bayern has focused on Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Forbes ranks Bayern as the world's fifth-most valuable football club in their <a href="/wiki/Forbes%27_list_of_the_most_valuable_football_clubs" title="Forbes' list of the most valuable football clubs">annual list</a>, estimating the club's value at <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1.235 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> As a result of Bayern's finals appearance in the 2012 UEFA Champions League, the club's brand value has reached US$786 million, up 59% from the previous year. Among European teams, this is ahead of Real Madrid's US$600 million and behind first-placed <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, whose brand is valued at US$853 million. In 2013, Bayern overtook Manchester United to take first place in brand valuation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_engagement_and_charity">Social engagement and charity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Social engagement and charity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bayern has been involved with charitable ventures for a long time, helping other football clubs in financial disarray as well as ordinary people in misery. In the wake of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake">2004 Tsunami</a> the "FC Bayern – Hilfe e.V." was founded, a foundation that aims to concentrate the social engagements of the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcbhilfe_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-fcbhilfe-135">[135]</a></sup> At its inception this venture was funded with €600,000, raised by officials and players of the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hiflfeathofh_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-hiflfeathofh-136">[136]</a></sup> The money was amongst other things used to build a school in Marathenkerny, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hiflfeathofh_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-hiflfeathofh-136">[136]</a></sup> and to rebuild the area of <a href="/wiki/Trincomalee" title="Trincomalee">Trincomalee</a>, Sri Lanka. In April 2007 it was decided that the focus of the foundation would shift towards supporting people in need locally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fcbhilfe_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-fcbhilfe-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club has also time and again shown to have a soft spot for clubs in financial disarray. Repeatedly the club has supported its local rival <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TSV_1860_M%C3%BCnchen" title="TSV 1860 München">1860 Munich</a> with gratuitous friendlies, transfers at favourable rates, and direct money transfers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Also when <a href="/wiki/FC_St._Pauli" title="FC St. Pauli">St. Pauli</a> threatened to lose its license for professional football due to financial problems, Bayern met the club for a friendly game free of any charge, giving all revenues to St. Pauli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> More recently when <a href="/wiki/Mark_van_Bommel" title="Mark van Bommel">Mark van Bommel</a>'s home club <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_Sittard" title="Fortuna Sittard">Fortuna Sittard</a> was in financial distress Bayern came to a charity game at the Dutch club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Another well known example was the transfer of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Zickler" title="Alexander Zickler">Alexander Zickler</a> in 1993 from <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_Dresden" title="Dynamo Dresden">Dynamo Dresden</a>. When Bayern picked up Zickler for 2.3 Million <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">DM</a> many considered the sum to be a subvention for the financially threatened <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_Dresden" title="Dynamo Dresden">Dresdeners</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In 2003, Bayern provided a 2 Million Euro loan without collateral to the nearly bankrupt <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> which has since been repaid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> On 14 July 2013, Bayern played a charity game against financially threatened third division Hansa Rostock. The game raised about €1 million, securing Hansa's licence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the summer of 2013 Bayern was the first club to give financial support to the <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Hirschfeld#Legacy" title="Magnus Hirschfeld">Magnus Hirschfeld National Foundation</a>. The foundation researches the living environment <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> people, and developed an education concept to facilitate unbiased dealing with LGBT themes in football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_facility">Training facility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Training facility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FCB_HQ-entrance.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2764" data-file-width="2040" height="298" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/FCB_HQ-entrance.JPG/220px-FCB_HQ-entrance.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/FCB_HQ-entrance.JPG/330px-FCB_HQ-entrance.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/FCB_HQ-entrance.JPG/440px-FCB_HQ-entrance.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FCB_HQ-entrance.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Entrance of Bayern Munich Headquarters</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>FC Bayern Munich training facilities, for both the professional and the <a href="/wiki/Bayern_Munich_Junior_Team" title="Bayern Munich Junior Team">Junior Team</a>, are located at the Bayern Munich Headquarters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-performancecentre_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-performancecentre-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youthacademy_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-youthacademy-147">[147]</a></sup> There are four grass pitches, one of which has undersoil heating, one artificial grass field and a multi-functional sports hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> After the closure of Munich American High School, FC Bayern purchased the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DoDDS" title="DoDDS">DoDDS</a> adjacent sporting fields that previously held MAHS's football pitch and baseball field. A new grass pitch was placed over the existing football pitch while an artificial turf field was placed over the baseball diamond.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FCB-Trainingsplatz.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/FCB-Trainingsplatz.JPG/220px-FCB-Trainingsplatz.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/FCB-Trainingsplatz.JPG/330px-FCB-Trainingsplatz.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/FCB-Trainingsplatz.JPG/440px-FCB-Trainingsplatz.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FCB-Trainingsplatz.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
FC Bayern Football pitch (training only)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The players' quarters opened in 1990 and were reconstructed after the 2007–08 season on suggestions by the new coach, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klinsmann" title="Jürgen Klinsmann">Jürgen Klinsmann</a>, who took inspiration from various major sports clubs. The quarters are now called the performance centre and feature a weights and fitness area, a massage unit, dressing rooms, the coaches' office, and a conference room with screening facilities for video analysis. A café, a library, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E-Learning" title="E-Learning">e-Learning</a> room, and a family room are also included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-performancecentre_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-performancecentre-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>Located at the headquarters is also the Youth academy, which houses up to 13 young talents from outside the city. While being part of Bayern's Junior Team they can work there on their development as footballers. Former residents of the Youth House include <a href="/wiki/Owen_Hargreaves" title="Owen Hargreaves">Owen Hargreaves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rensing" title="Michael Rensing">Michael Rensing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bastian_Schweinsteiger" title="Bastian Schweinsteiger">Bastian Schweinsteiger</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youthacademy_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-youthacademy-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006 Bayern purchased land near the Allianz Arena with the purpose of building a new youth academy. In 2015 the project, estimated to cost €70 million, was started, after overcoming internal resistance. The main reasons for the project were that the existing facilities were too small and that the club, while very successful at senior level, lacked competitiveness with other German and European clubs at youth level. The new facility is scheduled to open in the 2017–18 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_FC_Bayern_Munich_records_and_statistics#Honours" title="List of FC Bayern Munich records and statistics">List of FC Bayern Munich records and statistics § Honours</a></div>
<p>Bayern is historically the most successful team in German football, as they have won the most <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">championships</a> and the most <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">cups</a>. They are also Germany's most successful team in international competitions, having won eleven trophies. Bayern is one of only four clubs to have <a href="/wiki/UEFA_club_competition_records_and_statistics#List_of_teams_to_have_won_the_three_main_European_club_competitions" title="UEFA club competition records and statistics">won all three major European competitions</a> and also the last club to have won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> three times in a row, entitling them to wear a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_badge_of_honour" title="UEFA badge of honour">multiple-winner badge</a> during <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> matches.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bayern_hattrick_champions_league_trophies.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1296" data-file-width="2304" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bayern_hattrick_champions_league_trophies.jpg/220px-Bayern_hattrick_champions_league_trophies.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bayern_hattrick_champions_league_trophies.jpg/330px-Bayern_hattrick_champions_league_trophies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bayern_hattrick_champions_league_trophies.jpg/440px-Bayern_hattrick_champions_league_trophies.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

The three consecutive Champions League trophies won by FC Bayern Munich from 1974 to 1976. The one on the far right is the real trophy, given to Bayern permanently. The ones on the left are slightly smaller replicas.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic">Domestic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Domestic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">German Champions</a></b>
<ul>
<li><b>Winners</b> (26): <a href="/wiki/1932_German_football_championship" title="1932 German football championship">1931–32</a>, <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_Bundesliga" title="1968–69 Bundesliga">1968–69</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Bundesliga" title="1971–72 Bundesliga">1971–72</a>, <a href="/wiki/1972%E2%80%9373_Bundesliga" title="1972–73 Bundesliga">1972–73</a>, <a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_Bundesliga" title="1973–74 Bundesliga">1973–74</a>, <a href="/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_Bundesliga" title="1979–80 Bundesliga">1979–80</a>, <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Bundesliga" title="1980–81 Bundesliga">1980–81</a>, <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Bundesliga" title="1984–85 Bundesliga">1984–85</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_Bundesliga" title="1985–86 Bundesliga">1985–86</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Bundesliga" title="1986–87 Bundesliga">1986–87</a>, <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Bundesliga" title="1988–89 Bundesliga">1988–89</a>, <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Bundesliga" title="1989–90 Bundesliga">1989–90</a>, <a <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trebles">Trebles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Trebles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bayern Munich is the first and only team in Europe to have completed all available <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">Trebles</a> (continental treble, domestic treble and European treble).</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">Treble</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)#Annual_and_seasonal_trebles" title="Treble (association football)">Continental Treble</a> (<b><a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>, <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a></b>)
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="2012–13 FC Bayern Munich season">2012–2013</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)#National_trebles" title="Treble (association football)">Domestic Treble</a> (<b><a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>, <a href="/wiki/DFB-Pokal" title="DFB-Pokal">DFB-Pokal</a>, <a href="/wiki/DFL-Ligapokal" title="DFL-Ligapokal">DFB-Ligapokal</a></b>)
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_FC_Bayern_Munich_season" title="1999–2000 FC Bayern Munich season">1999–2000</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)#European_treble" title="Treble (association football)">European Treble</a> (<b><a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a></b>)
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/1966%E2%80%9367_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1966–67 European Cup Winners' Cup">1966–67 European Cup Winners' Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_European_Cup" title="1973–74 European Cup">1973–74 European Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_UEFA_Cup" title="1995–96 UEFA Cup">1995–96 UEFA Cup</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<p>At his farewell game, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Kahn" title="Oliver Kahn">Oliver Kahn</a> was declared honorary <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> of Bayern Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> The players below are part of the <b>FC Bayern Munich Hall of Fame</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coaches_since_1963">Coaches since 1963</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Coaches since 1963">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bayern had 19 coaches since its promotion to the Bundesliga in 1965. <a href="/wiki/Udo_Lattek" title="Udo Lattek">Udo Lattek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Trapattoni" title="Giovanni Trapattoni">Giovanni Trapattoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottmar_Hitzfeld" title="Ottmar Hitzfeld">Ottmar Hitzfeld</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jupp_Heynckes" title="Jupp Heynckes">Jupp Heynckes</a> served two terms as head coach. <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a> served one term as head coach and one as caretaker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Lattek was the club's most successful coach, having won six Bundeslige titles, two DFB Cups and the European Cup; following closely is Ottmar Hitzfeld, who won five Bundeslige titles, two DFB cups and the Champions League. The club's least successful coach was <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B8ren_Lerby" title="Søren Lerby">Søren Lerby</a>, who won less than a third of his matches in charge and presided over the club's near-relegation in the 1991–92 campaign.</p>
<p>The present manager, since July 2016, is <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ancelotti" title="Carlo Ancelotti">Carlo Ancelotti</a>, Real Madrid's former coach. On 20 December 2015, the club announced that Guardiola would not extend his contract beyond the end of the 2015–16 season. <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ancelotti" title="Carlo Ancelotti">Carlo Ancelotti</a> would be presented as his successor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pepretire_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-pepretire-161">[161]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_departments">Other departments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Other departments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FC_Bayern_II">FC Bayern II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: FC Bayern II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich_II" title="FC Bayern Munich II">FC Bayern Munich II</a></div>
<p>The reserve team serves mainly as the final stepping stone for promising young players before being promoted to the main team. Bayern II is coached by <a href="/wiki/Heiko_Vogel" title="Heiko Vogel">Heiko Vogel</a>, assisted by <a href="/wiki/Danny_Schwarz" title="Danny Schwarz">Danny Schwarz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rainer_Ulrich" title="Rainer Ulrich">Rainer Ulrich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Since the inception of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regionalliga_(football)" title="Regionalliga (football)">Regionalliga</a> in 1994, the team played in the <a href="/wiki/Regionalliga_S%C3%BCd" title="Regionalliga Süd">Regionalliga Süd</a>, after playing in the <a href="/wiki/Oberliga_(football)" title="Oberliga (football)">Oberliga</a> since 1978. In the 2007–08 season they qualified for the newly founded <a href="/wiki/3._Liga" title="3. Liga">3. Liga</a>, where they lasted until 2011, when they were relegated to the Regionalliga. This ended 33 consecutive years of playing in the highest league that the <a href="/wiki/German_Football_Association" title="German Football Association">German Football Association</a> permits the second team of a professional football team to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fussballdaten_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-fussballdaten-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Junior_football">Junior football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Junior football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bayern_Munich_Junior_Team" title="Bayern Munich Junior Team">Bayern Munich Junior Team</a></div>
<p>The <b>Bayern Munich Junior Team</b> has produced some of Europe's top football players, including <a href="/wiki/Owen_Hargreaves" title="Owen Hargreaves">Owen Hargreaves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hitzlsperger" title="Thomas Hitzlsperger">Thomas Hitzlsperger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Lahm" title="Philipp Lahm">Philipp Lahm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_M%C3%BCller" title="Thomas Müller">Thomas Müller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bastian_Schweinsteiger" title="Bastian Schweinsteiger">Bastian Schweinsteiger</a>. The division was founded in 1902 and is run by <a href="/wiki/Werner_Kern_(football_manager)" title="Werner Kern (football manager)">Werner Kern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Andersson" title="Björn Andersson">Björn Andersson</a>. It consists of eleven teams with more than 170 players, the youngest being under ten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women.27s_football">Women's football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Women's football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich_(women)" title="FC Bayern Munich (women)">FC Bayern Munich (women)</a></div>
<p>The women's football team which is led by head coach <a href="/wiki/Thomas_W%C3%B6rle" title="Thomas Wörle">Thomas Wörle</a> features several members of the German national youth team. In the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Bundesliga_(women)" title="2008–09 Bundesliga (women)">2008–09</a> season the team finished second in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(women)" title="Bundesliga (women)">women's Bundesliga</a>. The division was founded in 1970 and consists of four teams with 90 players. Their greatest successes were winning the <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_women%27s_football_champions" title="List of German women's football champions">championships</a> in 1976, 2015 and 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> In the 2011–12 season on 12 May 2012, FC Bayern Munich dethroned the German Cup title holders 1. FFC Frankfurt with a 2–0 in the 2011–12 final in Cologne and celebrated the biggest success of the club's history since winning the championship in 1976. In 2015 they won the Bundesliga for the first time, without any defeat. They won the 2015–16 Bundesliga, for the second time in a row.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">Other sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Other sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bayern has other departments<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otherdepartments_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-otherdepartments-11">[11]</a></sup> for:</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich_(basketball)" title="FC Bayern Munich (basketball)">FC Bayern Munich (basketball)</a></div>
<p>since 1946 with 280 players in 19 teams.<br/>
<i><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_champions_(basketball)" title="German champions (basketball)">German Champion</a></b></i> 1954,1955 and <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Basketball_Bundesliga" title="2013–14 Basketball Bundesliga">2014</a>, <i><b>German Cup</b></i> 1968</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bowling">Bowling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Bowling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>since 1984 with 46 players in 4 teams</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chess">Chess</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Chess">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>since 1908 with 97 players in 8 teams<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/European_Chess_Club_Cup" title="European Chess Club Cup">European Club Cup</a> 1992</p>
<p>German champion 1983, 1985, 1986, 1989, 1990, 1991, 1992, 1993 and 1995</p>
<p>German Fast chess champion 1984, 1985, 1987, 1988, 1989, 1990, 1991, 1992, 1993, 1994 and 1995 (record)</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gymnastics">Gymnastics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Gymnastics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>since 1974 with 35 gymnasts in 1 team</p>
<p>German champion 1983, 1986, 1987 and 1988</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Handball">Handball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Handball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>since 1945 with 3000 players in 10 teams</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Table_tennis">Table tennis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Table tennis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>since 1946 with 160 players in 12 teams</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Referees">Referees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Referees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>since 1919 with 115 referees</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_football">Senior football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Bayern_Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Senior football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>since 2001 with 135 players in 5 teams</p>

<li><b><a href="/wiki/2012_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2012 UEFA Super Cup">2012</a>:</b> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain"><img alt="Spain" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/15px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/30px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a></li>
